	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Northern (train operating company)</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the current Northern train operating company. For the former train operating company, see <a href="/wiki/Northern_Rail_(Serco-Abellio)" title="Northern Rail (Serco-Abellio)">Northern Rail (Serco-Abellio)</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">A British train company operating in Northern England</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><caption>Northern</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:ArrivaRailNorth.svg" class="image"><img October 2018</div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #efefef">Overview</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Franchise(s)</th><td>Northern<br />1 April 2016 – 31 March units<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;nb 1&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Stations called at</th><td>528</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Stations operated</th><td>476</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Parent company</th><td><a href="/wiki/Arriva_UK_Trains" title="Arriva UK Trains">Arriva UK Trains</a></td></tr><tr><th />.uk</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Northern</b> (legal name <b>Arriva Rail North Limited</b><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>) is a train operating company in <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">Northern England</a> which began operating the Northern franchise on 1 April 2016 and inherited units from the previous operator <a href="/wiki/Northern_Rail_(Serco-Abellio)" title="Northern Rail (Serco-Abellio)">Northern Rail</a>. A subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Arriva_UK_Trains" title="Arriva UK Trains">Arriva UK Trains</a>, Northern is the second-largest train franchise in the United Kingdom; its trains call at 528 stations – about a quarter of all stations in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Central to franchise commitments will be a £500 million investment in 101 new-built units – the <a href="/wiki/Class_195" class="mw-redirect" title="Class 195">Class 195</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_331" title="British Rail Class 331">331</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> These will be the first new-build trains for the Northern franchise since the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_333" title="British Rail Class 333">Class 333</a> in 2000 with further orders possible if the new units encourage passenger growth and improve passenger satisfaction.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The first units were introduced in July 2019 and the new rolling stock will enable all 102 <a href="/wiki/Pacer_(train)" title="Pacer (train)">Pacer trains</a> currently in service with Northern to be retired by the end of 2019. Additionally the <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_319" title="British Rail Class 319">Class 319</a> units will be replaced by the entire fleet of <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_323" title="British Rail Class 323">Class 323</a> units by 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-class323_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-class323-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It is also planned that a franchise sub-brand, known as <b><a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)#Northern_Connect" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern Connect</a></b>, will provide inter-urban services between major cities and towns in Northern England, as well as serving a number of major commuting stations. 
</p><p>Since the franchise began in April 2016, it has been beset by more late trains,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> poor customer service,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> frequent industrial action by staff,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> unpopular irregular calling patterns at commuter stations as part of timetable changes<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and delays in introducing new rolling stock.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Despite passenger growth at the vast majority of train operating companies in the United Kingdom and the Northern franchise operating more services<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;nb 2&#93;</a></sup>, the number of passengers carried since the franchise commenced in 2016 has declined; this has been attributed to worsening performance.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-arrivacrisis_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arrivacrisis-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The franchise will run to 2025 with an option for an additional year which is dependent on performance.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_(train_operating_company)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In August 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a> announced that <a href="/wiki/Abellio_(transport_company)" title="Abellio (transport company)">Abellio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arriva_UK_Trains" title="Arriva UK Trains">Arriva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Govia" title="Govia">Govia</a> had been shortlisted to bid for the next Northern franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The franchise was awarded to Arriva in December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Competition_and_Markets_Authority" title="Competition and Markets Authority">Competition and Markets Authority</a> launched an investigation into the transport department's decision to award the Northern network to Arriva.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Arriva operated the <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> franchise and owned many bus companies in the Northern trains operating area in which 'a significant overlap occurs without competition from other service providers.'<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Penalty_fares">Penalty fares</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_(train_operating_company)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Penalty fares">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As part of the new Franchise Agreement agreed in 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a> required the introduction of a penalty fare scheme across 60% of the Northern network by the end of 2019 and across the entire network by the end of 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-penaltyfareagreement_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-penaltyfareagreement-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Verification of this source citation failed to find it supporting or even relevant to the material that cites it (June 2019)">irrelevant citation</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The scheme aimed to reduce ticketless travel to less than 4.3% by March 2020 and 3.2% by March 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-penaltyfareagreement_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-penaltyfareagreement-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In April 2018, a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_fare" title="Penalty fare">penalty fare</a> scheme under the Railways (Penalty Fares) Regulations 2018 commenced to encourage passengers to purchase a ticket before boarding trains.
</p><p>As ticket machines at Northern managed stations do not accept cash, a 'Promise to Pay' notice system (similar to the <a href="/wiki/Permit_to_Travel" class="mw-redirect" title="Permit to Travel">Permit to Travel</a> ticketing system) is in operation. Customers who wish to purchase a ticket at an unmanned station of origin (i.e. either a closed, or no ticket office) with cash are required to collect a 'Promise to Pay' notice prior to boarding from a ticket machine. These notices can then be exchanged with the on-board conductor or with a member of railway staff at the destination station for a paid ticket.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Section 6 of the Railways (Penalty Fares) Regulations 2018 also covers a number of scenarios that prohibit penalty fares being issued such 'no facilities in operation for the sale of a travel ticket for that passenger's journey'.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="May_2018_timetable_recast">May 2018 timetable recast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_(train_operating_company)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: May 2018 timetable recast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Northern_passenger_journeys.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Northern_passenger_journeys.png/300px-Northern_passenger_journeys.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Northern_passenger_journeys.png/450px-Northern_passenger_journeys.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Northern_passenger_journeys.png/600px-Northern_passenger_journeys.png 2x" data-file-width="909" data-file-height="547" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northern_passenger_journeys.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Passenger journeys on Northern, 2010/11 to Q1 2017/18 (in millions, annual rolling average)<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arriva_Rail_North_(Northern_Rail)_-_Franchise_Performance_-_April_2016_to_April_2018.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Arriva_Rail_North_%28Northern_Rail%29_-_Franchise_Performance_-_April_2016_to_April_2018.png/300px-Arriva_Rail_North_%28Northern_Rail%29_-_Franchise_Performance_-_April_2016_to_April_2018.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Arriva_Rail_North_%28Northern_Rail%29_-_Franchise_Performance_-_April_2016_to_April_2018.png/450px-Arriva_Rail_North_%28Northern_Rail%29_-_Franchise_Performance_-_April_2016_to_April_2018.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Arriva_Rail_North_%28Northern_Rail%29_-_Franchise_Performance_-_April_2016_to_April_2018.png/600px-Arriva_Rail_North_%28Northern_Rail%29_-_Franchise_Performance_-_April_2016_to_April_2018.png 2x" data-file-width="6526" data-file-height="3658" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arriva_Rail_North_(Northern_Rail)_-_Franchise_Performance_-_April_2016_to_April_2018.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Northern Rail performance from commencement of franchise in April 2016 to November 2018. Graph generated from published period performance data by Arriva Rail North.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The franchise was widely criticised for implementing a new timetable in May 2018 which resulted in widespread delays and cancellations.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a> and Northern announced an independent inquiry to learn lessons and identify route alterations in readiness for the next timetable change in December 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In an attempt to counter operational problems, Northern implemented an emergency timetable on 4 June 2018<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> – it stemmed some delays and cancellations but was still problematic compared with performance before the timetable change.
</p><p>Punctuality was particularly bad in the North West due to the delay in the Blackpool–Preston electrification scheme, and the number of trains per hour through Manchester increased, with more trains using the <a href="/wiki/Ordsall_Chord" title="Ordsall Chord">Ordsall Chord</a> which became operational in December 2017. <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a> only informed train operating companies in January 2018 that the electrification scheme would be delayed until November; Northern had planned for the scheme to be complete as scheduled by May 2018 (it had already been postponed from Autumn 2017) and had trained drivers to operate new routes with electric rolling stock. Consequently, an alternative timetable had to be drafted up, and many train drivers were not sufficiently trained to drive the existing diesel rolling stock; this resulted in widespread cancellations.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, the additional services through the Manchester corridor resulted in increased congestion, and this had a knock-on effect.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Performance statistics published by the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Rail_and_Road" title="Office of Rail and Road">Office of Rail and Road</a> in October 2018 showed that from April to June 2018, the franchise recorded the lowest PPM – measured by train service departing within 5 minutes of its scheduled time – of any quarter since punctuality records began on the Northern franchise in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Performance later in 2018 continued to be poor, with many passengers protesting and a reduced service on Saturdays due to industrial action.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> In October 2018 it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Oxford_Road_railway_station" title="Manchester Oxford Road railway station">Manchester Oxford Road station</a>, the busiest station managed by Northern with over 8 million passengers, was the most delayed station in the United Kingdom in 2018 – this was attributed to the chaos following the May 2018 timetable.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Between 14 October and 10 November 2018, Northern recorded the worst monthly performance on record, with more trains late than on time. Less than 40% of services arrived <i>on time</i> (defined as services arriving within 59 seconds of the planned arrival time) and only 71.9% departed within 5 minutes of the scheduled departure time.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By November 2018, Arriva were re-evaluating their future involvement in the franchise due to a combination of declining passenger numbers as a result of the chaotic May 2018 timetable change and increasing compensation claims as a result of falling punctuality.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Both have pushed the franchise into financial losses and face<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (July 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> a £282 million government subsidy shortfall which was due to be passed onto the franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-arrivacrisis_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arrivacrisis-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Since the franchise commenced in April 2016 and despite an increase of 1,500 more weekly services transferred to Northern's operational remit, Northern has achieved no growth in passenger numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Between April and June 2018, the franchise suffered a 2.4% decline in passenger numbers compared with the previous year. Of the 22 train operating companies in the United Kingdom to record a fall in passengers, Northern were one of only three franchises to record a year-on-year drop in passenger numbers in 2017–18.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Statistics published in December 2018 showed that between April 2017 and March 2018, many Northern managed stations recorded a drop in passengers – this period did not include the May 2018 timetable change or the increased Saturday strikes by conductors.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Greater_Manchester" title="Mayor of Greater Manchester">Mayor of Greater Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andy_Burnham" title="Andy Burnham">Andy Burnham</a>, also reported that the failing railways in the region was resulting in increased congestion on the roads and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Metrolink" title="Manchester Metrolink">Metrolink</a> system, as passengers were abandoning the rail service as it had become less reliable since May 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> To counter continuing poor performance and encourage improved punctuality, the window for which passengers can claim compensation for delayed services was reduced from 30 minutes to 15 minutes from 17 December 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Minor changes were implemented in the December 2018 timetable change. However Northern said they did not expect a reliable service to be implemented until the May 2019 timetable change; it was expected that by this time there would be new rolling stock in service with the <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_195" title="British Rail Class 195">Class 195</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_331" title="British Rail Class 331">Class 331</a>, newly electrified lines operational which would alleviate the shortage of diesel rolling stock in the Northern fleet and most notably operational flaws with the May 2018 timetable ironed out as part of better optimised timetable in May 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="May_2019_and_new_trains">May 2019 and new trains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_(train_operating_company)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: May 2019 and new trains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:195WGN.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/195WGN.jpg/220px-195WGN.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/195WGN.jpg/330px-195WGN.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/195WGN.jpg/440px-195WGN.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:195WGN.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_195" title="British Rail Class 195">Class 195</a> units and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_331" title="British Rail Class 331">Class 331</a> were introduced in July 2019</div></div></div>
<p>In May 2019, further Northern Connect services were introduced, namely the Chester to Leeds service<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and the revised Manchester Airport to Barrow/Windermere service, to run via Wigan North Western. They also introduced an hourly service from Hull to Scarborough, doubling the service frequency on the Bridlington–Scarborough section of the line.
</p><p>However the May 2019 timetable does not include some of the improvements included in the original franchise agreement, such as a half-hourly service from Greenbank, Northwich, Knutsford and Altrincham to Stockport and Manchester; the additional Macclesfield and Poynton to Manchester and Blackpool service; or enhanced Sunday services.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Transport" title="Secretary of State for Transport">Transport Secretary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Grayling" title="Chris Grayling">Chris Grayling</a>, responded that "both Northern and Network Rail feel the additional paths cannot be accommodated without adversely affecting the reliability of other services on the network".<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2019, the Operator of Last Resort (managed by the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a>) conducted due diligence into the franchise believing the both operational and financial performance to be "unsustainable".<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Greater_Manchester" title="Mayor of Greater Manchester">Mayor of Greater Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andy_Burnham" title="Andy Burnham">Andy Burnham</a>, overtly demanded that the franchise be terminated as Northern have not delivered legally-binding franchise requirements as agreed in 2016 when the franchise commenced – citing disproportionate number of cancelled services, inability to deliver a full Sunday service due to a lack of drivers and failure to deliver new services.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 July 2019, the first nine units – seven <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_195" title="British Rail Class 195">Class 195</a> units and two <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_331" title="British Rail Class 331">Class 331</a> units – were introduced with a further 93 units to be introduced over the following 12 months. The initial roll-out commenced on three routes: Manchester Airport to Liverpool Lime Street and Barrow/Windermere and Leeds to Doncaster.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The franchise made a £21 million profit in 2016-17 and an £11.7 million profit in 2017-18 - a figure which does not include the fallout from the May 2018 timetable chaos.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> At the start of the franchise, it was agreed that there would be a subsidy of £275m in its first year and £260 in its third year - although Northern had received slightly more due to promised infrastructure improvements which the government had failed to deliver such as platforms 15 an 16 at <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_station" title="Manchester Piccadilly station">Manchester Piccadilly</a>. This was intended to fall sharply in 2020 to £221 million and by the end of the franchise in 2025 it would only receive £39 million.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to the planned sharp £39 million fall in subsidy in 2020 and which would push the franchise into a loss, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> was reported in summer 2019 that the Department of Transport viewed the franchise as "unsustainable" and were readying an Operator of Last Resort (OoLR) in the event the franchise collapses.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The franchise has struggled to increase passenger numbers and a challenge which was exacerbated by the fallout from the chaotic May 2018 timetable change.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_(train_operating_company)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northern_(train_operating_company)_routes" title="List of Northern (train operating company) routes">List of Northern (train operating company) routes</a></div>
<p>Northern took over all the services operated by <a href="/wiki/Northern_Rail_(Serco-Abellio)" title="Northern Rail (Serco-Abellio)">Northern Rail</a> (also branded Northern) on 1 April 2016<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and on the same date, services between <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_station" title="Manchester Airport station">Manchester Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_North_railway_station" title="Blackpool North railway station">Blackpool North</a>, Manchester Airport and <a href="/wiki/Barrow-in-Furness_railway_station" title="Barrow-in-Furness railway station">Barrow in Furness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oxenholme_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxenholme railway station">Oxenholme</a> to <a href="/wiki/Windermere_railway_station" title="Windermere railway station">Windermere</a> from <a href="/wiki/First_TransPennine_Express" title="First TransPennine Express">First TransPennine Express</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DfT270215_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DfT270215-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Northern took over responsibility for all the stations managed by Northern Rail, as well as <a href="/wiki/Arnside_railway_station" title="Arnside railway station">Arnside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barrow-in-Furness_railway_station" title="Barrow-in-Furness railway station">Barrow-in-Furness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birchwood_railway_station" title="Birchwood railway station">Birchwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burneside_railway_station" title="Burneside railway station">Burneside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnforth_railway_station" title="Carnforth railway station">Carnforth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grange-over-Sands_railway_station" title="Grange-over-Sands railway station">Grange-over-Sands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kendal_railway_station" title="Kendal railway station">Kendal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Staveley_railway_station" title="Staveley railway station">Staveley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ulverston_railway_station" title="Ulverston railway station">Ulverston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Central_railway_station" title="Warrington Central railway station">Warrington Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windermere_railway_station" title="Windermere railway station">Windermere</a> from First TransPennine Express.<sup id="cite_ref-DfT270215_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DfT270215-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Northern will staff some currently unstaffed stations. The first stations to be staffed will be <a href="/wiki/Baildon_railway_station" title="Baildon railway station">Baildon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ben_Rhydding_railway_station" title="Ben Rhydding railway station">Ben Rhydding</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-issuu.com_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-issuu.com-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> both in West Yorkshire.
</p><p>Northern has committed to introducing free <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a> on trains, and new ticketing options including the ability for customers to print their own tickets.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Arriva will provide new services across the North of England.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cleethorpes_railway_station" title="Cleethorpes railway station">Cleethorpes</a> to <a href="/wiki/Barton-on-Humber_railway_station" title="Barton-on-Humber railway station">Barton-on-Humber</a> service was due to be transferred to <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">East Midlands Railway</a> in August 2019 but will now not transfer until December 2019 .<sup id="cite_ref-DfT270215_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DfT270215-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The transfer will include <a href="/wiki/Barrow_Haven_railway_station" title="Barrow Haven railway station">Barrow Haven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barton_upon_Humber_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Barton upon Humber railway station">Barton upon Humber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goxhill_railway_station" title="Goxhill railway station">Goxhill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Coates_railway_station" title="Great Coates railway station">Great Coates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grimsby_Docks_railway_station" title="Grimsby Docks railway station">Grimsby Docks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Habrough_railway_station" title="Habrough railway station">Habrough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Healing_railway_station" title="Healing railway station">Healing</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Clee_railway_station" title="New Clee railway station">New Clee</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Holland_railway_station" title="New Holland railway station">New Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stallingborough_railway_station" title="Stallingborough railway station">Stallingborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thornton_Abbey_railway_station" title="Thornton Abbey railway station">Thornton Abbey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ulceby_railway_station" title="Ulceby railway station">Ulceby</a> stations.
</p><p>On 1 July 2016, the business was divided into four regions, each headed up by a regional director:<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><b>Central</b>&#160;– regional director based in Manchester</li>
<li><b>East</b>&#160;– regional director based in Leeds</li>
<li><b>North East</b>&#160;– regional director based in Newcastle upon Tyne</li>
<li><b>West</b>&#160;– regional director based in Preston</li></ul>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Table_of_off-peak_services">Table of off-peak services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_(train_operating_company)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Table of off-peak services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Below is a list of off-peak services, per the 30 June – 14 December 2019 timetables.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> It has been slightly simplified due to some routes' irregular service pattern. Due to the extensive nature of the network, it has been split by geographic area. Some services are listed in more than one place. Northern Connect lines are marked with their colour next to their route.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Connect"><span id="connect"></span>Northern Connect</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_(train_operating_company)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Northern Connect">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NorthernConnect.png" class="image"><img alt="Northern Connect logo" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/NorthernConnect.png/220px-NorthernConnect.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="74" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/96/NorthernConnect.png 1.5x" data-file-width="312" data-file-height="105" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NorthernConnect.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The logo for future Northern Connect express services</div></div></div>
<p>By December 2019, Northern plans to operate a network of twelve Northern Connect inter-urban express services – a franchise requirement. Most of these will be operated by brand-new <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_195" title="British Rail Class 195">Class 195 <i>Civity</i></a> diesel multiple units and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_331" title="British Rail Class 331">Class 331 <i>Civity</i></a> electric multiple units, whilst the <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_railway_station" title="Middlesbrough railway station">Middlesbrough</a> to <a href="/wiki/Carlisle_railway_station" title="Carlisle railway station">Carlisle</a> via <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station" title="Newcastle railway station">Newcastle</a> route will be operated by refurbished Class 158 units. Electrification of the line between <a href="/wiki/Oxenholme_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxenholme railway station">Oxenholme</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windermere_railway_station" title="Windermere railway station">Windermere</a> was cancelled by the Government in 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-railstaff0717_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railstaff0717-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> so the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Airport railway station">Manchester Airport</a> to Windermere route will be operated initially by <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_769" title="British Rail Class 769">Class 769 <i>Flex</i></a> trains instead, with <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_195" title="British Rail Class 195">Class 195</a> Civity trains taking over by the end of 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-railstaff0717_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railstaff0717-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Places that will be served by Northern Connect routes include <a href="/wiki/Bradford" title="Bradford">Bradford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chester" title="Chester">Chester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_West_Yorkshire" title="Halifax, West Yorkshire">Halifax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough" title="Middlesbrough">Middlesbrough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nottingham" title="Nottingham">Nottingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Preston,_Lancashire" title="Preston, Lancashire">Preston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barnsley" title="Barnsley">Barnsley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lincoln,_England" title="Lincoln, England">Lincoln</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wakefield" title="Wakefield">Wakefield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wigan" title="Wigan">Wigan</a> and <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a>.
</p><p><b>Northern Connect planned future routes and future rolling stock</b>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rolling_stock">Rolling stock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_(train_operating_company)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Rolling stock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Northern inherited the rolling stock operated by <a href="/wiki/Northern_Rail_(Serco-Abellio)" title="Northern Rail (Serco-Abellio)">Northern Rail</a>, namely Class <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_142" title="British Rail Class 142">142</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_144" title="British Rail Class 144">144</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_150" title="British Rail Class 150">150</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_153" title="British Rail Class 153">153</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_155" title="British Rail Class 155">155</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_156" title="British Rail Class 156">156</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_158" title="British Rail Class 158">158</a> <a href="/wiki/Diesel_multiple_unit" title="Diesel multiple unit">diesel multiple units</a> and Class <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_319" title="British Rail Class 319">319</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_321" title="British Rail Class 321">321</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_322" title="British Rail Class 322">322</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_323" title="British Rail Class 323">323</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_333" title="British Rail Class 333">333</a> <a href="/wiki/Electric_multiple_unit" title="Electric multiple unit">electric multiple units</a>. To operate services transferred from the <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> franchise, four <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_185" title="British Rail Class 185">Class 185</a> units were sublet from that franchise to Northern, with this later reducing to two units. As of the May 2019 timetable change, these sublet units have since returned to TPE. To provide additional peak time capacity on the <a href="/wiki/Calder_Valley_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Calder Valley Line">Calder Valley Line</a>, one <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_180" title="British Rail Class 180">Class 180</a> unit is sublet from <a href="/wiki/Grand_Central_(train_operating_company)" title="Grand Central (train operating company)">Grand Central</a> to Northern per weekday.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_37" title="British Rail Class 37">Class 37/4</a> locomotives and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Mark_2" class="mw-redirect" title="British Rail Mark 2">Mark 2 carriages</a> were hired from <a href="/wiki/Direct_Rail_Services" title="Direct Rail Services">Direct Rail Services</a> for <a href="/wiki/Cumbrian_Coast_line" title="Cumbrian Coast line">Cumbrian Coast line</a> services until December 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-DfT270215_61-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DfT270215-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first Class 142 train, 142005, was withdrawn from service on 12 August 2019<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>, with the remaining Class 142s due to be withdrawn before the end of the year.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_fleet">Future fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_(train_operating_company)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Future fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable floatright" style="font-size:95%">
<caption>Arriva Rail North Franchise Agreement Capacity Requirements<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>

<p>The withdrawal of <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_142" title="British Rail Class 142">Class 142</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_144" title="British Rail Class 144">144</a> trains, known commonly as <i>Pacers</i>, commenced on 12 August 2019, with the last to be removed from traffic during the first half of 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Other trains due to leave Northern's fleet are the <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_153" title="British Rail Class 153">Class 153</a> diesel multiple unit and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_319" title="British Rail Class 319">Class 319</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_321" title="British Rail Class 321">Class 321</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_322" title="British Rail Class 322">Class 322</a> electric multiple units.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>As part of the franchise agreement, there is a requirement to undertake refurbishment of all retained vehicles – these being the <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_150" title="British Rail Class 150">Class 150</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_155" title="British Rail Class 155">155</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_156" title="British Rail Class 156">156</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_158" title="British Rail Class 158">158</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_170" title="British Rail Class 170">170</a> diesel multiple units and the <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_319" title="British Rail Class 319">Class 319</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_323" title="British Rail Class 323">323</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_333" title="British Rail Class 333">333</a> electric multiple units. This includes new flooring and seat coverings, internal repaint, CCTV, Wi-Fi and provision of electric sockets. The sixteen <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_333" title="British Rail Class 333">Class 333</a> units were also to have two vehicles per set modified to a  “metro style” configuration to increase passenger carrying capacity per unit by at least 19%, but this did not materialise. The <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_319" title="British Rail Class 319">Class 319</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_333" title="British Rail Class 333">333</a> units are also to have pantograph monitoring equipment installed.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Northern has ordered 101 brand new trains from Spanish rolling stock manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Construcciones_y_Auxiliar_de_Ferrocarriles" title="Construcciones y Auxiliar de Ferrocarriles">CAF</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> A total of 58 <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_195" title="British Rail Class 195">Class 195</a> diesel multiple units and 43 <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_331" title="British Rail Class 331">Class 331</a> electric multiple units have been ordered and they started to enter service in July 2019.
</p><p>A number of other trains are to be cascaded to Northern from other operators. A total of 49 diesel trains are due to join the fleet from <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Railway_(train_operating_company)" title="Great Western Railway (train operating company)">Great Western Railway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abellio_ScotRail" title="Abellio ScotRail">ScotRail</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Midlands_Trains" title="West Midlands Trains">West Midlands Trains</a> between 2017 and 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> An additional eighteen two car diesel units, comparable to a <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_170" title="British Rail Class 170">Class 170</a>, are due to join the fleet by December 2022.
</p><p>In 2018, five <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_153" title="British Rail Class 153">Class 153</a> units transferred from <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Railway_(train_operating_company)" title="Great Western Railway (train operating company)">GWR</a> on a short term basis to provide extra capacity.
</p><p>An additional twelve <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_319" title="British Rail Class 319">Class 319</a> units have transferred from Thameslink, although eight of these are due to be converted to <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_769" title="British Rail Class 769">Class 769</a> bi mode multiple units.
</p><p>There is an option for further <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_195" title="British Rail Class 195">Class 195</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_331" title="British Rail Class 331">Class 331</a> carriages in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Originally, it was planned for Northern's Class 323 fleet to return to the leasing company, however, it was announced in August 2019 these would remain with Northern and be joined by <a href="/wiki/West_Midlands_Trains" title="West Midlands Trains">West Midlands Trains</a>' allocation of the type (26 units).<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Driver_Controlled_Operation">Driver Controlled Operation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_(train_operating_company)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Driver Controlled Operation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/One-man_operation#United_Kingdom" title="One-man operation">One-man operation</a></div>
<p>The Department of Transport and Rail North have specified that the franchise must ensure that at least 50% of the aggregate Train Mileage of Passenger Services provided in each Reporting Period is operated as Driver Controlled Operation (DCO).<sup id="cite_ref-railtechDCO_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railtechDCO-97">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>DCO is defined as "operation of a train by a driver alone without the need for a conductor (or any other Franchise Employee)." The franchise further specifies that "Where ... a Passenger Service is operated as Driver Controlled Operation the Franchisee shall ... plan for an additional Franchise Employee (that is, in addition to the driver) to be present on such Passenger Service."<sup id="cite_ref-NFA_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NFA-98">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Union_of_Rail,_Maritime_and_Transport_Workers" title="National Union of Rail, Maritime and Transport Workers">RMT Union</a> are unhappy about this change, as roles currently undertaken by guards would instead be undertaken by drivers (such as releasing the doors once the train has stopped at a station). Although Northern have said they would be willing to guarantee that a second member of staff would be on board, the use of DCO could theoretically make it possible to run a train without a guard, and as a result, the union have called industrial action over the change.<sup id="cite_ref-railtechDCO_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railtechDCO-97">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 28 November 2018 <a href="/wiki/Transport_for_the_North" title="Transport for the North">Transport for the North</a> announced that it did not support the removal of an additional franchise employee on Northern services, was willing to consider all options that would facilitate an agreement, and urged both Northern and the RMT Union to return to negotiations, suspending strike action.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> On 29 November, RMT announced that it had offered to suspend industrial action under the condition that trains will never run without a guard on the train,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> however, on 30 November, the union confirmed that it will continue industrial action as planned.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 6 February 2019, the RMT announced that following "a guarantee of a conductor on all trains, including the new fleet, for the duration of the current franchise" it had suspended further industrial action on Northern, bringing an end to consecutive strikes on Saturdays since 25 August 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Depots">Depots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_(train_operating_company)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Depots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Northern's fleet is maintained at <a href="/wiki/Allerton_TMD" title="Allerton TMD">Allerton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Botanic_Gardens_TMD" title="Botanic Gardens TMD">Botanic Gardens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heaton_TMD" title="Heaton TMD">Heaton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newton_Heath_TMD" title="Newton Heath TMD">Newton Heath</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neville_Hill_depot" class="mw-redirect" title="Neville Hill depot">Neville Hill</a> depots.
</p><p>In 2017, a new stabling depot opened at <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_King_Street_TMD" title="Blackburn King Street TMD">Blackburn King Street</a>, with space for up to thirty diesel multiple units.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A new depot will open in Wigan in December 2019, with space for 32 trains. The depot will be adapted from a freight yard at <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Springs_Branch_TMD" title="Wigan Springs Branch TMD">Springs Branch railway sidings</a> in Ince-in-Makerfield and will cost £46 million.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Northern currently has depots for its train crew at <a href="/wiki/Barrow-in-Furness_railway_station" title="Barrow-in-Furness railway station">Barrow-in-Furness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_railway_station" title="Blackburn railway station">Blackburn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_North_railway_station" title="Blackpool North railway station">Blackpool North</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buxton_railway_station" title="Buxton railway station">Buxton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlisle_railway_station" title="Carlisle railway station">Carlisle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darlington_railway_station" title="Darlington railway station">Darlington</a> (drivers), <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_railway_station" title="Doncaster railway station">Doncaster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harrogate_railway_station" title="Harrogate railway station">Harrogate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_railway_station" title="Huddersfield railway station">Huddersfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hull_Paragon_Interchange" title="Hull Paragon Interchange">Hull</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station" title="Liverpool Lime Street railway station">Liverpool Lime Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Piccadilly railway station">Manchester Piccadilly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Victoria railway station">Manchester Victoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_railway_station" title="Middlesbrough railway station">Middlesbrough</a> (guards), <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station" title="Newcastle railway station">Newcastle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield railway station">Sheffield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skipton_Broughton_Road_Carriage_sidings" title="Skipton Broughton Road Carriage sidings">Skipton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Wallgate_railway_station" title="Wigan Wallgate railway station">Wigan Wallgate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Workington_railway_station" title="Workington railway station">Workington</a> and <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_(train_operating_company)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">One unit is leased from <a href="/wiki/Grand_Central_(train_operating_company)" title="Grand Central (train operating company)">Grand Central</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The three services which transferred to the new Northern franchise in April 2016 are Manchester Airport to Blackpool North, Manchester Airport to Barrow-in-Furness and the Oxenholme to Windermere shuttle</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-74"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-74">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Six units are in warm storage and are not officially withdrawn from service.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-75">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">One morning peak time service from Hebden Bridge to Leeds, and one return trip in the evening peak, from Monday to Friday</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-77"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-77">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The eight Class 319/4 units are to be converted to Class 769 bi-mode units</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-86">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">These must be DMUs which are at least an equivalent in performance and quality to 2-car Class 170 units</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-87"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-87">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">These units must be in service no later than December 2022.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-91"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-91">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Class 319/4 units were initially built between 1987 and 1988</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-96"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-96">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Only one unit has been withdrawn as of September 2019, with a further six in warm storage.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
